## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology (population dynamics / growth ODE models)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is explicitly the time-derivative of population size P, indicating a population-growth differential equation. Classical ecology models relate dP_dt to density dependence (functions of P), environmental forcing (functions of t), and sometimes harvesting/immigration terms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited resources; per-capita growth constant)
- Affine source + proportional loss: dP_dt = c0 + c1 * P (constant immigration/emigration plus proportional growth/decline)
- Quadratic density dependence (Verhulst form as ODE): dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 (self-limitation via negative quadratic term when c1 < 0)
- Theta-logistic (generalized density dependence): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (nonlinear crowding; c2 tunes concavity of density dependence)
- Gompertz growth (continuous-time): dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (decelerating growth with logarithmic crowding)
- Richards / generalized logistic (shape parameter): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (P / c1))**c2 (flexible sigmoidal approach to carrying capacity)
- Allee effect (weak/strong): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - P / c2) (reduced growth at low density; bistability possible)
- Depensatory per-capita rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 / (P + c2)) (low-density suppression without explicit cubic term)
- Harvesting proportional to population: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P (net growth under proportional removal/mortality)
- Harvesting with saturation (Holling type II removal): dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P / (1 + c2 * P) (removal rate saturates at high P)
- Constant-yield harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / c1) - c2 (fixed offtake; risk of collapse when c2 large)
- Seasonally forced growth rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P (periodic environment affecting per-capita growth)
- Time-varying carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / (c1 + c2 * t)) (gradually changing resources/habitat)
- Pulsed/decaying environmental effect: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) * P - c3 * P**2 (transient forcing combined with crowding)
- Autonomous + external input: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / c1) + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (periodic immigration/resource subsidy)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Density dependence strength: linear-in-P per-capita rate (dP_dt/P = a + b*P) suggests quadratic terms in dP_dt; curvature in per-capita vs P suggests theta-logistic exponents.
- Carrying-capacity behavior: approaching a stable plateau in P over time typically implies a factor like (1 - P/K) or log(K/P) multiplying P in dP_dt.
- Allee effects: initial decline at low P followed by growth at intermediate P implies a (P - A) factor or other low-density suppression in dP_dt.
- Harvesting signatures: a constant downward shift in dP_dt across P indicates a constant-yield term (-H); a slope reduction proportional to P indicates proportional harvest (-h*P).
- Saturating removal/impact: diminishing marginal effect of P on negative terms (e.g., catch limits) suggests rational forms like P/(1+c*P) in subtraction.
- Seasonality/environmental forcing: repeating oscillations in dP_dt at similar P values across time indicate explicit t-dependent sinusoidal modulation of growth parameters.
- Nonstationary habitat/resources: systematic drift in equilibrium P over time implies time-varying parameters such as K(t) = c0 + c1*t or r(t) = c0 + c1*exp(c2*t).
- Finite-time blow-up vs bounded growth: rapidly accelerating dP_dt with increasing P (superlinear powers P**c, c>1) indicates potential runaway; bounded populations usually need negative higher-order terms.
- Scaling via per-capita rate: examining (dP_dt / P) often reveals whether the governing structure is additive in P (Gompertz/logistic family) versus additive in dP_dt (immigration/harvest).

============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (BPG18)
============================================================
GT: c0*P*sin(c1*t) + c2*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*P
Candidate formulas: 51

Let the GT be simplified first.

### Ground Truth (fixed function)
\[
\text{GT}=0.4770530111687279\,P\sin(0.7760602430275763\,t)+0.44545499474048156(1-P/51.06128580599878)P+0.44545499474048156P
\]
Expand the quadratic part:
\[
0.44545499474048156(1-P/c4)P = 0.44545499474048156P-\frac{0.44545499474048156}{51.06128580599878}P^2
\]
So
\[
\text{GT}= A\,P\sin(\omega t) + B\,P - D\,P^2
\]
with
- \(A=0.4770530111687279\)
- \(\omega=0.7760602430275763\)
- \(B=0.44545499474048156+0.44545499474048156=0.8909099894809631\)
- \(D=\frac{0.44545499474048156}{51.06128580599878}\) (a positive constant), so the \(P^2\) coefficient is \(-D\).

Thus any matching candidate must be able to represent exactly:
- one term \(P\sin(\omega t)\) with zero phase shift,
- plus a linear term in \(P\),
- plus a quadratic term in \(P\),
- and **no other dependence** on \(t\) or \(P\) (no exp, no max, no extra powers, no constants independent of \(P\), etc.).

---

## Candidate-by-candidate analysis

### 1. \(P c0 + P c1\sin(c2 t + c3) + P^{c4} c5 e^{c6 t}\)
To match GT, the last term must vanish for all \(t,P\): set \(c5=0\). Then we have \(Pc0 + Pc1\sin(c2 t + c3)\), but GT also needs a \(P^2\) term. Not possible. **No match**.

### 2. \(P^2 c0 + P c1 (c2+t)^{c3} + P c4\sin(c5 t + c6) + P c7\)
GT has no \((c2+t)^{c3}\) factor. To remove it for all \(t\), set \(c1=0\). Then we get \(P^2 c0 + P c4\sin(c5 t + c6)+Pc7\), which can match GT by choosing:
- \(c0=-D\)
- \(c4=A\)
- \(c5=\omega\)
- \(c6=0\)
- \(c7=B\)
All terms align exactly. **Match**.

### 3. \(P c0 (c1+t)^{c2} + P c3\sin(c4 t + c5) + P c6 (P c7 + 1)^{c8}\)
Need a pure linear-in-\(P\) term and a pure \(P^2\) term. The first term depends on \(t\) unless \(c2=0\) (then it becomes \(Pc0\)). The third term is generally nonlinear; to make it quadratic exactly, youâ€™d need \((Pc7+1)^{c8}\) to become affine in \(P\) (e.g., \(c8=1\)) giving \(P c6(Pc7+1)=c6c7 P^2 + c6 P\). That could work, but then youâ€™d have *two* independent linear \(P\) sources (from term1 and part of term3) which is fine (they can sum). Also need sine with zero phase: set \(c5=0\), \(c4=\omega\), \(c3=A\). Then choose:
- \(c2=0\) so term1 = \(Pc0\)
- \(c8=1\) so term3 = \(c6c7 P^2 + c6 P\)
Pick \(c6c7=-D\) and \(c0+c6=B\).
This seems feasible (take \(c6\neq 0\), \(c7=-D/c6\)). **Match**.

### 4. \(P^2 c0 + P c1 + P c2\sin(c3 t + c4) + P c5 + P c6\)
This is exactly \(P^2(\cdot)+P(\cdot)+P\sin(\cdot)\). Set:
- \(c0=-D\)
- \(c2=A\)
- \(c3=\omega\)
- \(c4=0\)
- \(c1+c5+c6=B\)
**Match**.

### 5. \(P^2 c0 + P c1 + P c2\sin(c3 t + c4)\)
Same structure as GT. Set:
- \(c0=-D\)
- \(c1=B\)
- \(c2=A\)
- \(c3=\omega\)
- \(c4=0\)
**Match**.

### 6. \(P^2 c0 + P c1 + P c2\sin(c3 t + c4) + P c5 + \max(0,-P+c6)\)
GT has no max term. Only way to remove it for all \(P\) is impossible because \(\max(0,-P+c6)\) cannot be identically 0 for all real \(P\) for any finite \(c6\). **No match**.

### 7. \(P c0 + P c1\sin(c2 t + c3) + P c4 (P c5)^{c6} + P c7\)
Need a \(P^2\) term: choose \(c6=1\) so third term is \(P c4 (P c5)=c4 c5 P^2\). Then set:
- \(c4 c5 = -D\)
- \(c0+c7 = B\)
- \(c1=A\), \(c2=\omega\), \(c3=0\)
**Match**.

### 8. \(P^2 c0 + P^2 c1 + P c2\sin(c3 + c4 t) + P c5\)
Combine \(P^2\) terms: coefficient \(c0+c1\). Sine phase: need \(c3=0\), \(c4=\omega\), \(c2=A\). Linear: \(c5=B\). Quadratic: \(c0+c1=-D\). **Match**.

### 9. \(P^2 c0 + P c1 + P c2\sin(c3 + c4 t) + \max(0,-P+c5)\)
Max term cannot be removed identically (same issue as #6). **No match**.

### 10. \(P^2 c0 + P c1 + P c2\sin(c3 t + c4) + P c5\)
Same as GT with linear split. Set \(c0=-D\), \(c1+c5=B\), \(c2=A\), \(c3=\omega\), \(c4=0\). **Match**.

### 11. \(P c0 + P c1\sin(c2 t + c3) + P^{c4} c5\)
To get a \(P^2\) term, set \(c4=2\), \(c5=-D\). Linear term \(Pc0\) gives \(B\) and sine term matches with \(c1=A,c2=\omega,c3=0\). **Match**.

### 12. \(P^2 c0 + P^2 c1 + P c2\sin(c3 + c4 t) + P c5 + P c6\)
Same as #8 with extra linear. Choose \(c0+c1=-D\), \(c2=A\), \(c3=0\), \(c4=\omega\), \(c5+c6=B\). **Match**.

### 13. \(P^2 c0 + P^2 c1 + P c2\sin(c3 + c4 t) + P c5 + P c6 + c6\max(0,-P+c7)\)
Even if you set the multiplier of max to 0 by choosing \(c6=0\), that also removes the \(P c6\) term, leaving \(P^2(c0+c1)+P c5 + P c2\sin(\cdot)\), which can still match GT (linear just uses \(c5=B\)). Also set \(c3=0,c4=\omega,c2=A,c0+c1=-D\). **Match**.

### 14. \(P c0 + P c1\sin(c2 t + c3) + P c4 (P c5)^{c6} + P c7 + c8 e^{c9 t}\)
Need no pure \(t\)-only exponential: set \(c8=0\). Then same as #7, which can match by \(c6=1\) etc. **Match**.

### 15. \(P^2 c0 + P^2 c1 + P c2 + P c3\sin(c4 + c5 t) + c6 e^{c7 t} + c8\max(0,-P+c9)\)
Remove unwanted terms: set \(c6=0\) and \(c8=0\). Then it becomes \(P^2(c0+c1)+P c2 + P c3\sin(c4+c5 t)\). Match with \(c0+c1=-D\), \(c2=B\), \(c3=A\), \(c5=\omega\), \(c4=0\). **Match**.

### 16. \(P c0 + P c1\sin(c2 t + c3) + P^{c4} c5 + c6 e^{c7 t}\)
Remove exponential: set \(c6=0\). Then same as #11, match with \(c4=2,c5=-D,c0=B,c1=A,c2=\omega,c3=0\). **Match**.

### 17. \(P c0 + P c1\sin(c2 t + c3) + P c4 (P c5)^{c6} + P c7 + c8 t^{c9}\)
Remove \(t^{c9}\): set \(c8=0\). Then same as #7. **Match**.

### 18. \(P^2 c0 + P c1 + P c2\sin(c3 t + c4) + P c5 + c6 t^{c7}\)
Remove \(t^{c7}\): set \(c6=0\). Then same as #10. **Match**.

### 19. \(P c0 + P c1\sin(c2 t + c3) + P c4 (P + c5)^{c6} + P c7 + c8 t^{c9}\)
Remove \(t^{c9}\): set \(c8=0\). Need quadratic: choose \(c6=1\) so third term is \(P c4(P+c5)=c4 P^2 + c4 c5 P\). Then pick \(c4=-D\), and adjust linear via \(c0+c7+c4 c5=B\). Sine matches with \(c1=A,c2=\omega,c3=0\). **Match**.

### 20. \(P c0 + P c1\sin(c2 t + c3) + P c4 (P c5 + 1)^{c6} + c7 t^{c8}\)
Remove \(t^{c8}\): set \(c7=0\). For quadratic, set \(c6=1\): third term \(P c4(P c5+1)=c4 c5 P^2 + c4 P\). Choose \(c4 c5=-D\) and \(c0+c4=B\). Sine as usual. **Match**.

### 21. \(P^2 c0 + P c1 + P c2\sin(c3 t + c4) + P c5 + c6 e^{c7 t}\)
Remove exponential: set \(c6=0\). Then same as #10. **Match**.

### 22. \(P c0 + P c1 + P c2 + P c3\sin(c4 t + c5) + P^{c6} c7 e^{c8 t} + c9\)
Need no constant term independent of \(P\): set \(c9=0\). Need no \(e^{c8 t}\) term: set \(c7=0\) (kills whole extra term). Then we have \(P(c0+c1+c2)+P c3\sin(c4 t + c5)\) but no \(P^2\) term. **No match**.

### 23. \(P^2 c0 + P c1 + P c2\sin(c3 t + c4) + P c5 + P c6 e^{c7 t}\)
To remove \(P e^{c7 t}\) for all \(t\), set \(c6=0\). Then same as #10. **Match**.

### 24. \(P^2 c0 + P^2 c1 + P c2 + P c3 + P c4\sin(c5 t + c6)\cos(c7 t) + c8\)
Need no constant: set \(c8=0\). The trig product generally produces multiple frequencies; to reduce to a single \(\sin(\omega t)\) term for all \(t\) is not possible unless you kill it (set \(c4=0\)), but then you lose the sine term required by GT. **No match**.

### 25. \(P c0 + P c1\sin(c2 t + c3) + P^{c4} c5 e^{c6 t} + c7 e^{c8 t}\)
Need no pure exponential: set \(c7=0\). Also need no \(e^{c6 t}\) in the \(P^{c4}\) term: set \(c6=0\). Then it becomes \(Pc0 + Pc1\sin(c2 t + c3) + P^{c4} c5\), same as #11, match with \(c4=2,c5=-D\), etc. **Match**.

### 26. \(P^2 c0 + P c1 + P c2\sin(c3 t + c4) + P c5 + c6 e^{c7 t} + \max(0,-P+c8)\)
Max term cannot be identically removed. **No match**.

### 27. \(P c0 + P c1 + P c2 + P c3\sin(c4 t + c5) + P c6 (P c7 + 1)^{c8} + c9\)
Need no constant: set \(c9=0\). For quadratic choose \(c8=1\): last term \(P c6(P c7+1)=c6 c7 P^2 + c6 P\). Then linear is \(P(c0+c1+c2+c6)\). Match with \(c6 c7=-D\), \(c0+c1+c2+c6=B\), sine with \(c3=A,c4=\omega,c5=0\). **Match**.

### 38. \(P^2 c0 + P^2 c1 + P c2 + P c3 + P c4 e^{P c5}\sin(c6 t + c7) + c8\)
The term \(P c4 e^{P c5}\sin(\cdot)\) introduces non-polynomial dependence on \(P\) unless \(c5=0\), making it \(P c4\sin(\cdot)\). Set \(c5=0\) and \(c8=0\). Then it becomes \(P^2(c0+c1)+P(c2+c3)+P c4\sin(c6 t + c7)\), which matches with \(c7=0,c6=\omega,c4=A,c0+c1=-D,c2+c3=B\). **Match**.

### 39. \(P c0 + P c1\sin(c2 t + c3) + P c4/(P + c5) + P c6 + P^{c7} c8\)
The rational term \(P c4/(P+c5)\) cannot become a polynomial \(\alpha P + \beta P^2\) for all \(P\) unless \(c4=0\) (kill it). Then we can set \(c7=2,c8=-D\) for quadratic, \(c0+c6=B\) for linear, sine matches. **Match**.

### 40. \(P c0 + P c1\sin(c2 t + c3) + P c4/(P + c5) + P c6 + P c7(P c8 + 1)^{c9}\)
Kill rational by \(c4=0\). For quadratic, set \(c9=1\): last term \(P c7(P c8+1)=c7 c8 P^2 + c7 P\). Then choose \(c7 c8=-D\), linear \(c0+c6+c7=B\), sine matches. **Match**.

### 41. \(P c0(c1+t)^{c2} + P c3(P c4)^{c5} + P c6\sin(c7 t + c8) + P c9\)

### 42. \(P^2 c0 + P c1 + P c2\sin(c3 t + c4) + P c5/(P + c6) + P c7 + P c8\)
Rational term must be removed: set \(c5=0\). Then itâ€™s \(P^2 c0 + P(\cdots)+P\sin(\cdot)\), match with \(c0=-D\), \(c2=A,c3=\omega,c4=0\), and \(c1+c7+c8=B\). **Match**.

### 43. \(P c0 + P c1\sin(c2 t + c3) + P^{c4} c5 e^{c6 t} + c7 t^{c8}\)
Remove \(t^{c8}\): set \(c7=0\). Remove \(e^{c6 t}\): set \(c6=0\). Then same as #11 with \(c4=2,c5=-D\). **Match**.

### 44. \(P^{3/4} c0 (c1 + P^{-1/4})^{c2} + P c3\sin(c4 + c5 t) + P c6 + c7/t\)
Has \(c7/t\) which cannot be identically 0 unless \(c7=0\) (ok). ### 45. \(P^3 c0 + P^2 c1 + P^2 c2 + P c3(c4+t)^{c5} + P c6 + P c7\sin(c8 t + c9)\)
Need no \(P^3\): set \(c0=0\). Need no \((c4+t)^{c5}\): set \(c3=0\). Then quadratic coefficient is \(c1+c2\) and we have linear \(Pc6\) and sine \(P c7\sin(\cdot)\). Match with \(c1+c2=-D\), \(c6=B\), \(c7=A,c8=\omega,c9=0\). **Match**.

### 46. \(P^3 c0 + P^2 c1 + P^2 c2 + P c3 + P c4\sin(c5 t + c6) + P c7\)
Set \(c0=0\). Quadratic \(c1+c2=-D\). Linear \(c3+c7=B\). Sine \(c4=A,c5=\omega,c6=0\). **Match**.

### 47. Same as 46 plus \(c8 t^{c9}\)
Set \(c0=0\) and remove \(t^{c9}\) by \(c8=0\). Then same as 46. **Match**.

### 48. Same as 46 plus \(c8 e^{c9 t}\)
Set \(c0=0\) and remove exponential by \(c8=0\). Then same as 46. **Match**.

### 49. \(P c0 + P c1\sin(c2 t + c3) + P c4\max(0,P c5 + 1)^{c6} + c7 e^{c8 t}\)
Remove exponential: set \(c7=0\). The max term is piecewise; to make it a polynomial globally, must avoid the kink. Only way is to make it constant 1 for all \(P\) (impossible) or kill it by \(c4=0\). If \(c4=0\), no \(P^2\) term. **No match**.

### 50. \(P c0 + P c1\sin(c2 t + c3) + P c4 e^{P c5} e^{c6 t} + c7 t^{c8}\)
Remove \(t^{c8}\): set \(c7=0\). The term \(P c4 e^{P c5} e^{c6 t}\) must vanish or become polynomial; to remove \(t\)-dependence set \(c6=0\), but still have \(P c4 e^{P c5}\), which is not polynomial unless \(c5=0\), giving \(P c4\) (linear only). Then no \(P^2\) term. If instead set \(c4=0\), term vanishes, still no \(P^2\). **No match**.

### 51. \(P c0 + P c1\sin(c2 t + c3) + P c4/(P c5 + c6) + c7/(P c5 + c6) + c8 t^{c9}\)
Remove \(t^{c9}\): set \(c8=0\). The rational terms cannot become a polynomial in \(P\) for all \(P\) unless their numerators are zero: set \(c4=0\) and \(c7=0\). Then left with \(P c0 + P c1\sin(\cdot)\) and no \(P^2\) term. **No match**.
